## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science (solid mechanics / thermomechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables indicate a constitutive relation for stress (sigma) as a function of strain (epsilon) with temperature (T) affecting elastic modulus, yield/flow stress, and strain-hardening/softening. Common models combine an elastic (often linear) response in epsilon with temperature-dependent material parameters and sometimes nonlinear hardening or saturation in epsilon.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic softening/stiffening with T)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (quadratic): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (curved E(T) behavior)
- Thermoelastic strain shift (thermal expansion compensation): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - (c1 * T + c2)) (stress from mechanical strain after thermal strain subtraction)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (finite-strain/nonlinear elasticity approximation)
- Coupled polynomial in strain with T-dependent coefficients: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (temperature-modified nonlinearity)
- Power-law hardening (Hollomon-type): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic flow with scale-free hardening)
- Power-law with temperature-dependent strength: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (thermal softening/stiffening of flow stress)
- Ludwik-type offset + hardening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + c2 * epsilon**c3 (yield/offset stress plus strain hardening with T dependence)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (hardening that saturates at large strain)
- Temperature-modulated Voce term: sigma = c0 + (c1 * exp(c2 * T)) * (1 - exp(-c3 * epsilon)) (T changes saturation magnitude or rate)
- Hockett–Sherby-type saturation: sigma = c0 + (c1 - c0) * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon**c3)) (flexible saturation curvature in plasticity)
- Thermally activated strength (activation-like dependence): sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * exp(c3 / (T + c4)) (strength increases as T decreases via activation term)
- Logarithmic strain dependence (empirical hardening): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + c2 * log(epsilon + c3) (often used for limited strain ranges)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification: sigma proportional to epsilon suggests Hookean behavior; the proportionality factor is an effective modulus that may vary with T.
- Thermal expansion effects: appearance of (epsilon - (c*T + c)) indicates stress driven by mechanical strain after subtracting thermal strain.
- Thermal softening/stiffening of modulus or strength: coefficients multiplying epsilon or adding an offset that decrease with T capture softening; linear/quadratic in T often fits moderate ranges.
- Strain hardening signatures: sigma growing like epsilon**c reflects power-law hardening; larger exponent implies more rapid hardening at higher strain.
- Saturating hardening: (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or (1 - exp(-c*epsilon**p)) indicates approach to an asymptotic flow stress at large epsilon.
- Curvature change with temperature: allowing hardening prefactors like c*exp(c*T) captures that work-hardening rate or saturation stress changes strongly with T.
- Low-temperature strengthening via activation-like terms: exp(c/(T+c)) produces rapid increases as T decreases, consistent with thermally activated barriers.
- Nonlinear elasticity vs plasticity clue: higher-order polynomial terms in epsilon often represent elastic nonlinearity at moderate strains, while offset-plus-hardening terms suggest elastic-plastic flow stress modeling.

- `T**2*c0*epsilon` in candidate 48

**None of the candidates have `T*epsilon**3`** as a term. The GT requires this cross term, and it cannot be generated from any combination of the basis functions present in the candidates.

For candidates with `T*c0`: This gives a term linear in T but independent of epsilon, whereas the GT needs `T*epsilon**3`. These are linearly independent functions and cannot match.

For candidate 48 with `T**2*epsilon`: This is also different from `T*epsilon**3`.

The term `epsilon**0.2 * exp(-c/T)` in the GT is also problematic. In the candidates, the T-dependent terms are things like `exp(T*c)`, `1/sqrt(T)`, `1/T**3`, `log(T*c+1)` - none of which involve `exp(-c/T)`. And the epsilon-dependent terms are separate from T-dependent terms (no products).

**Critical issue:** The GT has terms where epsilon and T are **multiplied together** (both `T*epsilon**3` and `epsilon**0.2*exp(-c/T)`), but ALL candidates have terms that are **either** functions of epsilon alone **or** functions of T alone (they are additively separable in epsilon and T). No candidate has any product of epsilon-dependent and T-dependent terms.

Since the GT is NOT additively separable in epsilon and T, and all candidates ARE additively separable, no candidate can match.

Let me verify candidate 48: `T**2*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**(1/5) + c3*epsilon**c4 + c5*sqrt(epsilon) + c6*epsilon**(1/3) + c7*epsilon**4 + c8*epsilon**2` - this has `T**2*epsilon` but no `T*epsilon**3`, and no exponential in T at all. Cannot match.
